## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is typical of constitutive laws for elastic/plastic deformation with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield stress, and thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (Hooke with temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with E(T))
- Elastic with reciprocal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (T + c1) (stiffness decreases with increasing temperature)
- Quadratic/nonlinear elastic (Murnaghan-type truncation): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate-strain nonlinear elasticity with thermal dependence)
- Cubic elastic nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (phenomenological nonlinearity; temperature shifts effective modulus)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (E(T) following an exponential trend; c1 often negative)
- Thermal activation-like softening of flow stress (exponential): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (plastic/flow stress scaling in strain with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (strain hardening with temperature-shifted prefactor)
- Ramberg–Osgood (inverse form, stress from strain): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma**c2 (nonlinear elastic-plastic curve fit; usable when solving for sigma numerically)
- Swift/Hollomon-type hardening with temperature-shifted strain offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (work hardening with pre-strain and temperature effect)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (empirical hardening times thermal softening factor)
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain embedded: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T + c2) (linear stress vs mechanical strain where thermal strain is proportional to T)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic surrogate (smooth transition): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + Abs(epsilon)) + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon (captures initial linearity then saturation/hardening with temperature dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: use (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon or c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) to encode monotonic softening/stiffening with T.
- Thermal softening bounded near melting/transition: use factors like (c0 + c1 * T)**c2 or c0 / (T + c1) to prevent unphysical growth at high T.
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain: add higher powers in epsilon (epsilon**2, epsilon**3) with coefficients that may depend on T.
- Plastic hardening behavior: represent sigma increasing sublinearly/superlinearly with epsilon via epsilon**c or (epsilon + c)**c, optionally scaled by a T-dependent prefactor.
- Separable hardening × softening structure: use sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) to reflect multiplicative decomposition often used in empirical constitutive fits.
- Thermal strain shift: include (epsilon + c0 * T + c1) inside the stress law to represent stress-free thermal expansion offset.
- Avoid negative stress at small tensile strain: include offsets like (epsilon + c0)**c1 (with c0 > 0) rather than pure epsilon**c when fractional powers are possible.
- Transition from elastic to plastic: use rational forms like c0 * epsilon / (c1 + Abs(epsilon)) added to a linear term to mimic an initial linear regime followed by reduced incremental stiffness.
